# big-code-pg-arch-001: PostgreSQL Query Execution Pipeline

## Task

Trace the PostgreSQL query execution pipeline from parse to execute. Starting from `exec_simple_query()` in the traffic cop, map how a SQL string flows through the parser (lexer + grammar), semantic analyzer, query rewriter, planner/optimizer, and executor, identifying the data structures that flow between each stage.

## Context

- **Repository**: postgres/postgres (C, ~1.5M LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: src/backend/ — parser, rewrite, optimizer, executor subsystems

## Requirements

1. Identify all files involved in the query pipeline (traffic cop, parser, analyzer, rewriter, planner, executor, node type definitions)
2. Trace the dependency chain from `exec_simple_query()` through each pipeline stage, identifying the data type transformations (RawStmt -> Query -> PlannedStmt -> tuples)
3. Document the two-phase optimization (Path generation via allpaths.c, then Plan creation via createplan.c)
4. Explain the Volcano-style executor dispatch in execProcnode.c

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — role in architecture
- path/to/file2.ext — role in architecture
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Entry point: path/to/entry.ext
2. Calls: path/to/next.ext (via function/method name)
3. Delegates to: path/to/impl.ext
...

## Analysis
[Detailed architectural analysis including:
- Design patterns identified
- Component responsibilities
- Data flow description
- Interface contracts between components]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary answering the task question]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find the correct set of architecturally relevant files?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct dependency/call chain?
- Architectural coherence: Did you correctly identify the design patterns and component relationships?

  1011→exec_simple_query(const char *query_string)
  1012→{
  1013→	CommandDest dest = whereToSendOutput;
  1014→	MemoryContext oldcontext;
  1015→	List	   *parsetree_list;
  1016→	ListCell   *parsetree_item;

  1018→	bool		was_logged = false;
  1019→	bool		use_implicit_block;
  1020→	char		msec_str[32];
  1021→
  1022→	/*
  1023→	 * Report query to various monitoring facilities.
  1024→	 */
  1025→	debug_query_string = query_string;
  1026→

  1028→

  1030→
  1031→	/*
  1032→	 * We use save_log_statement_stats so ShowUsage doesn't report incorrect
  1033→	 * results because ResetUsage wasn't called.
  1034→	 */
  1035→	if (save_log_statement_stats)
  1036→		ResetUsage();
  1037→
  1038→	/*
  1039→	 * Start up a transaction command.  All queries generated by the
  1040→	 * query_string will be in this same command block, *unless* we find a
  1041→	 * BEGIN/COMMIT/ABORT statement; we have to force a new xact command after
  1042→	 * one of those, else bad things will happen in xact.c. (Note that this
  1043→	 * will normally change current memory context.)
  1044→	 */
  1045→	start_xact_command();
  1046→
  1047→	/*
  1048→	 * Zap any pre-existing unnamed statement.  (While not strictly necessary,
  1049→	 * it seems best to define simple-Query mode as if it used the unnamed
  1050→	 * statement and portal; this ensures we recover any storage used by prior
  1051→	 * unnamed operations.)
  1052→	 */
  1053→	drop_unnamed_stmt();
  1054→
  1055→	/*
  1056→	 * Switch to appropriate context for constructing parsetrees.
  1057→	 */
  1058→	oldcontext = MemoryContextSwitchTo(MessageContext);
  1059→

   603→pg_parse_query(const char *query_string)
   604→{
   605→	List	   *raw_parsetree_list;
   606→
   607→	TRACE_POSTGRESQL_QUERY_PARSE_START(query_string);
   608→
   609→	if (log_parser_stats)
   610→		ResetUsage();
   611→
   612→	raw_parsetree_list = raw_parser(query_string, RAW_PARSE_DEFAULT);

   619→	/* Optional debugging check: pass raw parsetrees through copyObject() */

   621→	{
   622→		List	   *new_list = copyObject(raw_parsetree_list);
   623→
   624→		/* This checks both copyObject() and the equal() routines... */
   625→		if (!equal(new_list, raw_parsetree_list))
   626→			elog(WARNING, "copyObject() failed to produce an equal raw parse tree");
   627→		else
   628→			raw_parsetree_list = new_list;
   629→	}
   630→

   632→	 * Optional debugging check: pass raw parsetrees through
   633→	 * outfuncs/readfuncs
   634→	 */
   635→	if (Debug_write_read_parse_plan_trees)
   636→	{
   637→		char	   *str = nodeToStringWithLocations(raw_parsetree_list);
   638→		List	   *new_list = stringToNodeWithLocations(str);
   639→
   640→		pfree(str);
   641→		/* This checks both outfuncs/readfuncs and the equal() routines... */
   642→		if (!equal(new_list, raw_parsetree_list))
   643→			elog(WARNING, "outfuncs/readfuncs failed to produce an equal raw parse tree");
   644→		else
   645→			raw_parsetree_list = new_list;
   646→	}
   647→
   648→#endif							/* DEBUG_NODE_TESTS_ENABLED */
   649→
   650→	TRACE_POSTGRESQL_QUERY_PARSE_DONE(query_string);
   651→
   652→	return raw_parsetree_list;
   653→}

   970→pg_plan_queries(List *querytrees, const char *query_string, int cursorOptions,
   971→				ParamListInfo boundParams)
   972→{
   973→	List	   *stmt_list = NIL;
   974→	ListCell   *query_list;
   975→
   976→	foreach(query_list, querytrees)
   977→	{
   978→		Query	   *query = lfirst_node(Query, query_list);
   979→		PlannedStmt *stmt;
   980→
   981→		if (query->commandType == CMD_UTILITY)
   982→		{
   983→			/* Utility commands require no planning. */
   984→			stmt = makeNode(PlannedStmt);
   985→			stmt->commandType = CMD_UTILITY;
   986→			stmt->canSetTag = query->canSetTag;
   987→			stmt->utilityStmt = query->utilityStmt;
   988→			stmt->stmt_location = query->stmt_location;
   989→			stmt->stmt_len = query->stmt_len;
   990→			stmt->queryId = query->queryId;
   991→		}
   992→		else
   993→		{
   994→			stmt = pg_plan_query(query, query_string, cursorOptions,
   995→								 boundParams);
   996→		}
   997→
   998→		stmt_list = lappend(stmt_list, stmt);
   999→	}
  1000→
  1001→	return stmt_list;
  1002→}

   882→pg_plan_query(Query *querytree, const char *query_string, int cursorOptions,
   883→			  ParamListInfo boundParams)
   884→{
   885→	PlannedStmt *plan;
   886→
   887→	/* Utility commands have no plans. */
   888→	if (querytree->commandType == CMD_UTILITY)
   889→		return NULL;
   890→
   891→	/* Planner must have a snapshot in case it calls user-defined functions. */
   892→	Assert(ActiveSnapshotSet());
   893→
   894→	TRACE_POSTGRESQL_QUERY_PLAN_START();
   895→
   896→	if (log_planner_stats)
   897→		ResetUsage();
   898→
   899→	/* call the optimizer */
   900→	plan = planner(querytree, query_string, cursorOptions, boundParams);
   901→
   902→	if (log_planner_stats)
   903→		ShowUsage("PLANNER STATISTICS");
   904→

   907→	/* Optional debugging check: pass plan tree through copyObject() */

39-usertext-
I need to trace the PostgreSQL query execution pipeline to identify all relevant files. Here's what I know so far:

1. Entry point: exec_simple_query() in src/backend/tcop/postgres.c (line 1011)
2. Parse stage: pg_parse_query() -> raw_parser() (the lexer/parser)
3. Analyze & Rewrite stage: pg_analyze_and_rewrite_fixedparams() -> parse_analyze_fixedparams() and pg_rewrite_query()
4. Plan stage: pg_plan_queries() -> pg_plan_query() -> planner() (optimizer)
5. Execute stage: PortalStart() and PortalRun()

Key data structures:
- RawStmt (output of parser)
- Query (output of analyzer/rewriter)
- PlannedStmt (output of planner)
- Plan nodes (various execution nodes)

Please find and list:
1. The definition of raw_parser() function and its location
2. The definition of parse_analyze_fixedparams() and its location
3. The definition of pg_rewrite_query() and its location
4. The definition of planner() and its location
5. The main optimizer files mentioned: allpaths.c, createplan.c
6. Executor files, especially execProcnode.c which implements Volcano-style dispatch
7. Node type definitions for RawStmt, Query, PlannedStmt, Plan

Use a medium thoroughness level and search in src/backend/parser, src/backend/optimizer, src/backend/executor, src/backend/nodes directories.

     1→/*-------------------------------------------------------------------------
     2→ *
     3→ * parsenodes.h
     4→ *	  definitions for parse tree nodes
     5→ *
     6→ * Many of the node types used in parsetrees include a "location" field.
     7→ * This is a byte (not character) offset in the original source text, to be
     8→ * used for positioning an error cursor when there is an error related to
     9→ * the node.  Access to the original source text is needed to make use of
    10→ * the location.  At the topmost (statement) level, we also provide a
    11→ * statement length, likewise measured in bytes, for convenience in
    12→ * identifying statement boundaries in multi-statement source strings.
    13→ *
    14→ *

     1→/*-------------------------------------------------------------------------
     2→ *
     3→ * execProcnode.c
     4→ *	 contains dispatch functions which call the appropriate "initialize",
     5→ *	 "get a tuple", and "cleanup" routines for the given node type.
     6→ *	 If the node has children, then it will presumably call ExecInitNode,
     7→ *	 ExecProcNode, or ExecEndNode on its subnodes and do the appropriate
     8→ *	 processing.
     9→ *
    10→ * Portions Copyright (c) 1996-2025, PostgreSQL Global Development Group
    11→ * Portions Copyright (c) 1994, Regents of the University of California
    12→ *
    13→ *
    14→ * IDENTIFICATION
    15→ *	  src/backend/executor/execProcnode.c
    16→ *
    17→ *-------------------------------------------------------------------------
    18→ */
    19→/*
    20→ *	 NOTES
    21→ *		This used to be three files.  It is now all combined into
    22→ *		one file so that it is easier to keep the dispatch routines
    23→ *		in sync when new nodes are added.
    24→ *
    25→ *	 EXAMPLE
    26→ *		Suppose we want the age of the manager of the shoe department and
    27→ *		the number of employees in that department.  So we have the query:
    28→ *
    29→ *				select DEPT.no_emps, EMP.age
    30→ *				from DEPT, EMP
    31→ *				where EMP.name = DEPT.mgr and
    32→ *					  DEPT.name = "shoe"
    33→ *
    34→ *		Suppose the planner gives us the following plan:
    35→ *
    36→ *						Nest Loop (DEPT.mgr = EMP.name)
    37→ *						/		\
    38→ *					   /		 \
    39→ *				   Seq Scan		Seq Scan
    40→ *					DEPT		  EMP
    41→ *				(name = "shoe")
    42→ *
    43→ *		ExecutorStart() is called first.
    44→ *		It calls InitPlan() which calls ExecInitNode() on
    45→ *		the root of the plan -- the nest loop no

   105→parse_analyze_fixedparams(RawStmt *parseTree, const char *sourceText,
   106→						  const Oid *paramTypes, int numParams,
   107→						  QueryEnvironment *queryEnv)
   108→{
   109→	ParseState *pstate = make_parsestate(NULL);
   110→	Query	   *query;
   111→	JumbleState *jstate = NULL;
   112→
   113→	Assert(sourceText != NULL); /* required as of 8.4 */
   114→
   115→	pstate->p_sourcetext = sourceText;
   116→
   117→	if (numParams > 0)
   118→		setup_parse_fixed_parameters(pstate, paramTypes, numParams);
   119→
   120→	pstate->p_queryEnv = queryEnv;
   121→
   122→	query = transformTopLevelStmt(pstate, parseTree);
   123→
   124→	if (IsQueryIdEnabled())
   125→		jstate = JumbleQuery(query);
   126→
   127→	if (post_parse_analyze_hook)
   128→		(*post_parse_analyze_hook) (pstate, query, jstate);
   129→
   130→	free_parsestate(pstate);
   131→
   132→	pgstat_report_query_id(query->queryId, false);
   133→
   134→	return query;
   135→}

   354→	 * the planner don't bother with that stuff, but we must have it on the

Excellent! I've successfully completed the comprehensive architectural analysis of the PostgreSQL query execution pipeline. Here's a summary of what I've documented:

## Key Findings

### **Files Identified** (80+ critical files)
- **Traffic Cop:** `src/backend/tcop/postgres.c` — entry point `exec_simple_query()`
- **Parser:** `src/backend/parser/parser.c` — `raw_parser()` with flex/bison
- **Analyzer:** `src/backend/parser/analyze.c` — `parse_analyze_fixedparams()`
- **Rewriter:** `src/backend/rewrite/` — rule application and view expansion
- **Optimizer (Phase 1):** `src/backend/optimizer/path/allpaths.c` — Path generation
- **Optimizer (Phase 2):** `src/backend/optimizer/plan/createplan.c` — Plan creation
- **Executor:** `src/backend/executor/execProcnode.c` — Volcano-style dispatch + 40+ node types

### **Dependency Chain** (Complete Call Sequence)
```
exec_simple_query() 
  → raw_parser() [RawStmt]
  → parse_analyze_fixedparams() [Query]
  → pg_rewrite_query() [Query list]
  → planner()/standard_planner() [PlannedStmt]
    - Phase 1: subquery_planner() → allpaths.c generates Paths
    - Phase 2: create_plan() converts best Path → Plan tree
  → ExecutorStart() → ExecInitNode() [PlanState tree]
  → ExecutorRun() → ExecProcNode() [Tuples via Volcano model]
```

### **Key Architectural Patterns Identified**
1. **Pipeline Architecture:** Clean separation of stages (parse→analyze→rewrite→optimize→execute)
2. **Two-Phase Optimization:** Logical (allpaths.c) + Physical (createplan.c) separation
3. **Volcano/Iterator Model:** Function pointer dispatch for runtime tuple fetching
4. **Hybrid Dispatch:** Switch statement at init (line 161, execProcnode.c) + function pointers at runtime
5. **Cost-Based Optimization:** Dynamic programming with selectivity estimation
6. **Modular

"     1\u2192/*-------------------------------------------------------------------------\n     2\u2192 *\n     3\u2192 * execProcnode.c\n     4\u2192 *\t contains dispatch functions which call the appropriate \"initialize\",\n     5\u2192 *\t \"get a tuple\", and \"cleanup\" routines for the given node type.\n     6\u2192 *\t If the node has children, then it will presumably call ExecInitNode,\n     7\u2192 *\t ExecProcNode, or ExecEndNode on its subnodes and do the appropriate\n     8\u2192 *\t processing.\n     9\u2192 *\n    10\u2192 * Portions Copyright (c) 1996-2025, PostgreSQL Global Development Group\n    11\u2192 * Portions Copyright (c) 1994, Regents of the University of California\n    12\u2192 *\n    13\u2192 *\n    14\u2192 * IDENTIFICATION\n    15\u2192 *\t  src/backend/executor/execProcnode.c\n    16\u2192 *\n    17\u2192 *-------------------------------------------------------------------------\n    18\u2192 */\n    19\u2192/*\n    20\u2192 *\t NOTES\n    21\u2192 *\t\tThis used to be three files.  It is now all combined into\n    22\u2192 *\t\tone file so that it is easier to keep the dispatch routines\n    23\u2192 *\t\tin sync when new nodes are added.\n    24\u2192 *\n    25\u2192 *\t EXAMPLE\n    26\u2192 *\t\tSuppose we want the age of the manager of the shoe department and\n    27\u2192 *\t\tthe number of employees in that department.  So we have the query:\n    28\u2192 *\n    29\u2192 *\t\t\t\tselect DEPT.no_emps, EMP.age\n    30\u2192 *\t\t\t\tfrom DEPT, EMP\n    31\u2192 *\t\t\t\twhere EMP.name = DEPT.mgr and\n    32\u2192 *\t\t\t\t\t  DEPT.name = \"shoe\"\n    33\u2192 *\n    34\u2192 *\t\tSuppose the planner gives us the following plan:\n    35\u2192 *\n    36\u2192 *\t\t\t\t\t\tNest Loop (DEPT.mgr = EMP.name)\n    37\u2192 *\t\t\t\t\t\t/\t\t\\\n    38\u2192 *\t\t\t\t\t   /\t\t \\\n    39\u2192 *\t\t\t\t   Seq Scan\t\tSeq Scan\n    40\u2192 *\t\t\t\t\tDEPT\t\t  EMP\n    41\u2192 *\t\t\t\t(name = \"shoe\")\n    42\u2192 *\n    43\u2192 *\t\tExecutorStart() is called first.\n    44\u2192 *\t\tIt calls InitPlan() which calls ExecInitNode() on\n    45\u2192 *\t\tthe root of the plan -- the nest loop node.\n    46\u2192 *\n    47\u2192 *\t  * ExecInitNode() notices that it is looking at a nest loop and\n    48\u2192 *\t\tas the code below demonstrates, it calls ExecInitNestLoop().\n    49\u2192 *\t\tEventually this calls ExecInitNode() on the right and left subplans\n    50\u2192 *\t\tand so forth until the entire plan is initialized.  The result\n    51\u2192 *\t\tof ExecInitNode() is a plan state tree built with the same structure\n    52\u2192 *\t\tas the underlying plan tree.\n    53\u2192 *\n    54\u2192 *\t  * Then when ExecutorRun() is called, it calls ExecutePlan() which calls\n    55\u2192 *\t\tExecProcNode() repeatedly on the top node of the plan state tree.\n    56\u2192 *\t\tEach time this happens, ExecProcNode() will end up calling\n    57\u2192 *\t\tExecNestLoop(), which calls ExecProcNode() on its subplans.\n    58\u2192 *\t\tEach of these subplans is a sequential scan so ExecSeqScan() is\n    59\u2192 *\t\tcalled.  The slots returned by ExecSeqScan() may contain\n    60\u2192 *\t\ttuples which contain the attributes ExecNestLoop() uses to\n    61\u2192 *\t\tform the tuples it returns.\n    62\u2192 *\n    63\u2192 *\t  * Eventually ExecSeqScan() stops returning tuples and the nest\n    64\u2192 *\t\tloop join ends.  Lastly, ExecutorEnd() calls ExecEndNode() which\n    65\u2192 *\t\tcalls ExecEndNestLoop() which in turn calls ExecEndNode() on\n    66\u2192 *\t\tits subplans which result in ExecEndSeqScan().\n    67\u2192 *\n    68\u2192 *\t\tThis should show how the executor works by having\n    69\u2192 *\t\tExecInitNode(), ExecProcNode() and ExecEndNode() dispatch\n    70\u2192 *\t\ttheir work to the appropriate node support routines which may\n    71\u2192 *\t\tin turn call these routines themselves on their subplans.\n    72\u2192 */\n    73\u2192#include \"postgres.h\"\n    74\u2192\n    75\u2192#include \"executor/executor.h\"\n    76\u2192#include \"executor/nodeAgg.h\"\n    77\u2192#include \"executor/nodeAppend.h\"\n    78\u2192#include \"executor/nodeBitmapAnd.h\"\n    79\u2192#include \"executor/nodeBitmapHeapscan.h\"\n    80\u2192#include \"executor/nodeBitmapIndexscan.h\"\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.     "content": "/*-------------------------------------------------------------------------\n *\n * execProcnode.c\n *\t contains dispatch functions which call the appropriate \"initialize\",\n *\t \"get a tuple\", and \"cleanup\" routines for the given node type.\n *\t If the node has children, then it will presumably call ExecInitNode,\n *\t ExecProcNode, or ExecEndNode on its subnodes and do the appropriate\n *\t processing.\n *\n * Portions Copyright (c) 1996-2025, PostgreSQL Global Development Group\n * Portions Copyright (c) 1994, Regents of the University of California\n *\n *\n * IDENTIFICATION\n *\t  src/backend/executor/execProcnode.c\n *\n *-------------------------------------------------------------------------\n */\n/*\n *\t NOTES\n *\t\tThis used to be three files.  It is now all combined into\n *\t\tone file so that it is easier to keep the dispatch routines\n *\t\tin sync when new nodes are added.\n *\n *\t EXAMPLE\n *\t\tSuppose we want the age of the manager of the shoe department and\n *\t\tthe number of employees in that department.  So we have the query:\n *\n *\t\t\t\tselect DEPT.no_emps, EMP.age\n *\t\t\t\tfrom DEPT, EMP\n *\t\t\t\twhere EMP.name = DEPT.mgr and\n *\t\t\t\t\t  DEPT.name = \"shoe\"\n *\n *\t\tSuppose the planner gives us the following plan:\n *\n *\t\t\t\t\t\tNest Loop (DEPT.mgr = EMP.name)\n *\t\t\t\t\t\t/\t\t\\\n *\t\t\t\t\t   /\t\t \\\n *\t\t\t\t   Seq Scan\t\tSeq Scan\n *\t\t\t\t\tDEPT\t\t  EMP\n *\t\t\t\t(name = \"shoe\")\n *\n *\t\tExecutorStart() is called first.\n *\t\tIt calls InitPlan() which calls ExecInitNode() on\n *\t\tthe root of the plan -- the nest loop node.\n *\n *\t  * ExecInitNode() notices that it is looking at a nest loop and\n *\t\tas the code below demonstrates, it calls ExecInitNestLoop().\n *\t\tEventually this calls ExecInitNode() on the right and left subplans\n *\t\tand so forth until the entire plan is initialized.  The result\n *\t\tof ExecInitNode() is a plan state tree built with the same structure\n *\t\tas the underlying plan tree.\n *\n *\t  * Then when ExecutorRun() is called, it calls ExecutePlan() which calls\n *\t\tExecProcNode() repeatedly on the top node of the plan state tree.\n *\t\tEach time this happens, ExecProcNode() will end up calling\n *\t\tExecNestLoop(), which calls ExecProcNode() on its subplans.\n *\t\tEach of these subplans is a sequential scan so ExecSeqScan() is\n *\t\tcalled.  The slots returned by ExecSeqScan() may contain\n *\t\ttuples which contain the attributes ExecNestLoop() uses to\n *\t\tform the tuples it returns.\n *\n *\t  * Eventually ExecSeqScan() stops returning tuples and the nest\n *\t\tloop join ends.  Lastly, ExecutorEnd() calls ExecEndNode() which\n *\t\tcalls ExecEndNestLoop() which in turn calls ExecEndNode() on\n *\t\tits subplans which result in ExecEndSeqScan().\n *\n *\t\tThis should show how the executor works by having\n *\t\tExecInitNode(), ExecProcNode() and ExecEndNode() dispatch\n *\t\ttheir work to the appropriate node support routines which may\n *\t\tin turn call these routines themselves on their subplans.\n */\n#include \"postgres.h\"\n\n#include \"executor/executor.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeAgg.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeAppend.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeBitmapAnd.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeBitmapHeapscan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeBitmapIndexscan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeBitmapOr.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeCtescan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeCustom.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeForeignscan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeFunctionscan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeGather.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeGatherMerge.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeGroup.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeHash.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeHashjoin.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeIncrementalSort.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeIndexonlyscan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeIndexscan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeLimit.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeLockRows.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeMaterial.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeMemoize.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeMergeAppend.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeMergejoin.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeModifyTable.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeNamedtuplestorescan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeNestloop.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeProjectSet.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeRecursiveunion.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeResult.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeSamplescan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeSeqscan.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeSetOp.h\"\n#include \"executor/nodeSort.h\"\n#include 'node'.\n *\n *\t\tInputs:\n *\t\t  'node' is the current node of the plan produced by the query planner\n *\t\t  'estate' is the shared execution state for the plan tree\n *\t\t  'eflags' is a bitwise OR of flag bits described in executor.h\n *\n *\t\tReturns a PlanState node corresponding to the given Plan node.\n * ------------------------------------------------------------------------\n tree.\n\t */\n\tif (node == NULL)\n\t\treturn NULL;\n\n\t/*\n\t * Make sure there's enough stack available. Patterns Identified\n\n#### 1. **Pipeline/Dataflow Architecture**\nThe query execution is organized as a strict pipeline with clear stages:\n- **Parse**: Syntax validation and raw AST production\n- **Analyze**: Semantic validation and reference resolution\n- **Rewrite**: Rule application and query transformation\n- **Optimize**: Logical and physical optimization\n- **Execute**: Tuple production via iterator model\n\nEach stage produces well-defined intermediate data structures:\n```\nSQL String \u2192 RawStmt \u2192 Query \u2192 PlannedStmt \u2192 PlanState Tree \u2192 Tuples\n```\n\n#### 2. **Two-Phase Optimization (Separation of Concerns)**\n\n**Phase 1 - Path Generation (Logical):** `src/backend/optimizer/path/allpaths.c`\n- Generates multiple candidate execution strategies (Paths)\n- Focus: logical correctness and cost estimation\n- Dynamic programming for join order selection\n- Cost-based pruning keeps only viable alternatives\n- Output: RelOptInfo with pathlist\n\n**Phase 2 - Plan Creation (Physical):** `src/backend/optimizer/plan/createplan.c`\n- Selects best Path, converts to Plan tree\n- Maps logical operators to physical operators\n- Attaches implementation details (sort orders, output columns)\n- Line 395-414: Dispatch via `switch (best_path->pathtype)` converts Path\u2192Plan\n\n**Benefits:**\n- Cost model independent of plan generation\n- Easy to add new plan types without changing all paths\n- Clean separation between logical and physical optimization\n\n#### 3. **Volcano/Iterator Model (Push-up from Leaves)**\n\n**Initialization Phase (Bottom-up construction):**\n- ExecInitNode recursively builds state tree\n- Each node knows its specific ExecProcNode function\n- Mirrors plan tree structure in memory\n\n**Execution Phase (Top-down fetching):**\n```\nfor each result_tuple needed:\n  tup = ExecProcNode(top_node)  // Call iterator function\n  // Recursively:\n  //   ExecProcNode(top_node) \u2192 ExecNestLoop \u2192 calls ExecProcNode(children)\n  //   When all outer tuples: stop\n```\n\n**Function Pointer Dispatch (not switch statement):**\n```c\nExecSetExecProcNode(result, result->ExecProcNode);  // Line 391, execProcnode.c\n// Each node's ExecInit* sets result->ExecProcNode to node-specific function:\n// ExecSeqScan, ExecIndexScan, ExecNestLoop, ExecHashJoin, ExecAgg, etc.\n\n// At runtime:\nTupleTableSlot *slot = (*planstate->ExecProcNode)(planstate);  // Call via pointer\n```\n\n**Advantages:**\n- Minimal overhead (function pointer vs switch)\n- Natural pipelining (tuples flow up the tree)\n- Easy to plug in new node types (just add ExecInit*/Exec* functions)\n\n#### 4. **Dispatcher Pattern with Static and Dynamic Dispatch Hybrid**\n\nAt initialization time (static dispatch via switch):\n```c\nswitch (nodeTag(node)):  // Line 161, execProcnode.c\n  case T_SeqScan:\n    result = ExecInitSeqScan(...);\n    break;\n  case T_NestLoop:\n    result = ExecInitNestLoop(...);\n    break;\n  // 40+ cases\n```\n\nAt runtime (dynamic dispatch via function pointers):\n```c\n(*planstate->ExecProcNode)(planstate)  // No switch, just indirect call\n```\n\n**Benefit:** Fast initialization path uses switch (compiler can optimize), fast execution uses function pointers (cache-friendly).\n\n#### 5. **Node Type System (Tagged Union)**\nAll AST and plan node types tagged with NodeTag enum:\n```c\ntypedef enum NodeTag {\n  T_RawStmt, T_SelectStmt, T_Query, T_Plan, T_SeqScan, T_NestLoop, ...\n} NodeTag;\n\n// Every node starts with:\ntypedef struct SomeNode {\n  NodeTag type;\n  ...\n} SomeNode;\n```\n\nEnables:\n- Runtime type checking via `IsA(node, type)`\n- Polymorphic node operations (copy, compare, print)\n- Generic node traversal\n\n#### 6. **Recursive Tree Processing**\nPlan/Path trees are inherently recursive:\n- ExecInitNode recursively processes children\n- create_plan recursively processes child paths\n- ExecEndNode recursively finalizes children\n- Maximizes code reuse and maintains tree structure\n\n#### 7. **Cost-Based Optimization with Heuristic Pruning**\n\nDynamic programming with pruning (joinrels.c, allpaths.c):\n- Enumerate join orders using DP algorithm\n- At each DP step, keep only best paths for each relation subset\n- For large n, use GEQO (genetic algorithm) as fallback\n- Result: Tractable optimization despite exponential search space\n\n#### 8. **Separation of Planning from Execution**\n\nPlan nodes are immutable during execution:\n- No side effects during planning\n- Transaction semantics isolated in executor\n- Allows plan caching (prepared statements)\n- Multiple executions of same plan possible\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n**Traffic Cop (postgres.c):**\n- Receives raw SQL from client\n- Coordinates pipeline stages\n- Manages transaction context\n- Implements portal interface\n\n**Parser (parser/parser.c + lex/gram.y):**\n- Lexical analysis (flex)\n- Syntactic analysis (bison)\n- No semantic checking, no table access\n- Input: SQL string; Output: RawStmt list\n\n**Analyzer (parser/analyze.c + parse_*.c):**\n- Semantic validation\n- Name resolution (tables, columns, functions)\n- Type checking and coercion\n- Input: RawStmt; Output: Query\n\n**Rewriter (rewrite/rewriteHandler.c):**\n- Apply view expansion\n- Apply INSTEAD rules\n- Apply row-level security policies\n- Input: Query; Output: Query list (possibly expanded)\n\n**Optimizer Path Generation (optimizer/path/allpaths.c):**\n- Generate candidate access paths\n- Estimate costs using selectivity estimation\n- Consider index availability\n- Dynamic programming for join orders\n- Output: RelOptInfo with Path alternatives\n\n**Optimizer Plan Creation (optimizer/plan/createplan.c):**\n- Select best Path\n- Convert Path to Plan tree\n- Attach implementation details\n- Output: Plan tree\n\n**Executor Initialization (executor/execProcnode.c, ExecInitNode):**\n- Build state tree from plan tree\n- Set up runtime execution context\n- Initialize per-node state (buffers, cursors, etc.)\n- Output: PlanState tree with function pointers\n\n**Executor Runtime (executor/nodeXxx.c, ExecProcNode):**\n- Fetch tuples via Volcano model\n- Implement join algorithms (nested loop, merge, hash)\n- Implement grouping/aggregation\n- Implement sorting (when needed)\n- Output: TupleTableSlots with result tuples\n\n### Data Flow Description\n\n```\n1. PARSE PHASE (Traffic Cop \u2192 Parser)\n   Input:  SELECT a, b FROM table WHERE x > 5\n   Process: Lexer tokenizes \u2192 Parser builds syntax tree\n   Output: RawStmt { SelectStmt { ... } }\n\n2. ANALYZE PHASE (Traffic Cop \u2192 Analyzer)\n   Input:  RawStmt { SelectStmt { table: \"table\", ... } }\n   Process:\n     - Resolve \"table\" to RangeTableEntry (catalog lookup)\n     - Resolve \"a\", \"b\", \"x\" to actual columns\n     - Check types (b > 5 requires compatible types)\n   Output: Query {\n     rtable: [RTE for \"table\"],\n     targetList: [Var(a), Var(b)],\n     jointree: FromExpr with WHERE x > 5\n   }\n\n3. REWRITE PHASE (Traffic Cop \u2192 Rewriter)\n   Input:  Query { ... }\n   Process:\n     - Check if \"table\" is a view \u2192 if so, expand to underlying query\n     - Check for INSTEAD rules \u2192 apply if present\n     - Apply row-level security filters\n   Output: Query (possibly modified or expanded to multiple queries)\n\n4. OPTIMIZE PHASE (Phase 1: Paths)\n   Input:  Query { rtable: [...], conditions: [x > 5], ... }\n   Process:\n     - RelOptInfo for \"table\" created\n     - Generate Paths:\n       * SeqScan Path (read all rows)\n       * IndexScan Path (if index on x exists)\n     - Estimate costs based on stats\n     - Choose best Path (likely IndexScan if x > 5 is selective)\n   Output: Path tree with costs\n\n5. OPTIMIZE PHASE (Phase 2: Plans)\n   Input:  Path tree (best SeqScan or IndexScan)\n   Process:\n     - Convert Path to Plan node\n     - Attach output columns (a, b)\n   Output: Plan tree:\n     SeqScan {\n       relationName: \"table\",\n       targetList: [Var(a), Var(b)],\n       filter: (x > 5)\n     }\n\n6. EXECUTOR INIT PHASE (Executor \u2192 Init)\n   Input:  Plan tree\n   Process:\n     - ExecInitNode called recursively on plan tree\n     - For SeqScan: creates SeqScanState with scan iterator\n     - Sets SeqScanState->ExecProcNode = ExecSeqScan\n   Output: PlanState tree with function pointers set\n\n7. EXECUTOR RUN PHASE (Executor \u2192 Run)\n   Process:\n     for tuple_count > 0:\n       slot = ExecProcNode(top_planstate)  // Call ExecSeqScan\n       if slot is NULL: break\n       tuple = extract_tuple(slot)\n       send_to_client(tuple)\n\n   Inside ExecSeqScan():\n     - Read next page from buffer manager\n     - Extract next tuple matching filter (x > 5)\n     - Return tuple in TupleTableSlot or NULL when done\n\n8. Output: Result tuples sent to client\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts Between Components\n\n| Stage | Function | Input | Output | Invariants |\n|-------|----------|-------|--------|-----------|\n| Parser | `raw_parser()` | SQL string | `List<RawStmt>` | No semantic checking; may contain invalid tables/columns |\n| Analyzer | `parse_analyze_fixedparams()` | `RawStmt` | `Query` | All names resolved; types checked; references valid |\n| Rewriter | `pg_rewrite_query()` | `Query` | `List<Query>` | May expand to multiple queries; maintains semantic equivalence |\n| Optimizer | `planner()` | `Query` | `PlannedStmt` | Plan is executable; all Paths explored and best selected |\n| Executor | `ExecutorStart()` | `PlannedStmt` | `PlanState` | PlanState tree ready for iteration; ExecProcNode pointers set |\n| Executor | `ExecProcNode()` | `PlanState` | `TupleTableSlot` | Tuple or NULL; called repeatedly until NULL |\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nPostgreSQL's query execution pipeline is a sophisticated multi-stage system implementing classical compilation and execution architecture patterns. The **pipeline/dataflow design** organizes processing into well-separated stages (parse, analyze, rewrite, optimize, execute), each with clean input/output interfaces and well-defined intermediate representations (RawStmt \u2192 Query \u2192 PlannedStmt \u2192 tuples).\n\nThe **two-phase optimization** (path generation in allpaths.c + plan creation in createplan.c) cleanly separates logical optimization (which strategies are possible?) from physical optimization (which strategy is fastest?). This enables cost-based selection while maintaining code modularity and extensibility.\n\nThe **Volcano/iterator execution model** combined with **hybrid static/dynamic dispatch** achieves both simplicity and performance: initialization uses a switch statement for optimal startup, while execution uses function pointers for minimal per-tuple overhead and natural pipelining through the plan tree. The 40+ executor node types (scans, joins, aggregation, sorting, etc.) all follow this pattern, making it easy to add new node types without modifying core executor logic.",

\u251c\u2500 T_Agg, T_Group, ... \u2192 create_group_plan()\n     \u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 ... Portal Creation & Execution\n**File:** `src/backend/tcop/postgres.c` (line 1215)\n**Function:** `CreatePortal()` \u2014 Create unnamed portal\n**Function:** `PortalDefineQuery()` \u2014 Associate plantree_list with portal\n**Function:** `PortalStart()` \u2014 Initialize portal\n\n### 6. Execution Stage (Tuple Production)\n**File:** `src/backend/executor/execMain.c`\n**Function:** `ExecutorStart(QueryDesc, int eflags)` \u2192 `InitPlan()`\n\n#### Executor Initialization (Bottom-up tree construction)\n```\nExecutorStart()\n  \u2514\u2500 InitPlan(estate, plannedstmt)\n     \u2502\n     \u2514\u2500 ExecInitNode(root_plan, estate, eflags)  [execProcnode.c:142]\n        \u2502\n        \u251c\u2500 switch (nodeTag(node)):  [line 161, 40+ cases]\n        \u2502  \u251c\u2500 T_SeqScan \u2192 ExecInitSeqScan() \u2192 create SeqScanState\n        \u2502  \u251c\u2500 T_IndexScan \u2192 ExecInitIndexScan() \u2192 create IndexScanState\n        \u2502  \u251c\u2500 T_NestLoop \u2192 ExecInitNestLoop() \u2192 recursively init children\n        \u2502  \u251c\u2500 T_HashJoin \u2192 ExecInitHashJoin() \u2192 init hash table builder\n        \u2502  \u251c\u2500 T_Agg \u2192 ExecInitAgg() \u2192 init aggregation state\n        \u2502  \u2514\u2500 ... [one case per Plan node type]\n        \u2502\n        \u251c\u2500 ExecSetExecProcNode(result, result->ExecProcNode)\n        \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Sets function pointer: result->ExecProcNode = ExecSeqScan (or node-specific)\n        \u2502\n        \u2514\u2500 Recursively call ExecInitNode() on child plans\n           \u2514\u2500 Build parallel PlanState tree (mirrors Plan tree)\n```\n\n**Data Structures:**\n- `Plan` (plan-time structure) \u2192 `PlanState` (runtime structure)\n- Each PlanState has:\n  - `ExecProcNode` function pointer (specific tuple-fetching function)\n  - State for that node (e.g., scan position, aggregate buffer)\n  - Links to child PlanStates\n\n#### Executor Iteration (Top-down tuple fetching)\n```\nExecutorRun(queryDesc, direction, count)\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 ExecutePlan(estate, planstate, ...) \u2014 Main execution loop\n  \u2502  \u2502\n  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 for each tuple needed:\n  \u2502     \u2502\n  \u2502     \u2514\u2500 ExecProcNode(top_planstate)  [Volcano model]\n  \u2502        \u2502\n  \u2502        \u251c\u2500 Calls function pointer: (*planstate->ExecProcNode)(planstate)\n  \u2502        \u2502  \u2514\u2500 e.g., ExecSeqScan(planstate) \u2192 fetches next heap tuple\n  \u2502        \u2502\n  \u2502        \u2514\u2500 Returns TupleTableSlot with tuple or NULL (end)\n  \u2502           \u2502\n  \u2502           \u251c\u2500 If leaf node (SeqScan):\n  \u2502           \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Reads from heap pages via buffer manager\n  \u2502           \u2502\n  \u2502           \u251c\u2500 If join node (NestLoop):\n  \u2502           \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Calls ExecProcNode(outer_child)\n  \u2502           \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Calls ExecProcNode(inner_child) for each outer tuple\n  \u2502           \u2502\n  \u2502           \u2514\u2500 If aggregation node (Agg):\n  \u2502              \u251c\u2500 Accumulates tuples in hash/sort aggregation state\n  \u2502              \u2514\u2500 Returns aggregate results when input exhausted\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500 Apply output tuple sink (copy to client buffer via printtup)\n  \u2514\u2500 return tuple count\n```\n\n**Execution Model:** Volcano/Iterator model\n- Each node is a generator (ExecProcNode)\n- Child calls are pull-based (parent calls child repeatedly)\n- Tuples flow bottom-up through plan tree\n- Natural pipelining with buffering only at specific points (sorts, hash joins)\n\n#### Executor Finalization\n```\nExecutorEnd(queryDesc)\n  \u2502\n  \u2514\u2500 ExecEndNode(top_planstate)  [execProcnode.c, ExecEndNode case]\n     \u2502\n     \u251c\u2500 switch (nodeTag(plan)):  [Dispatch to node-specific cleanup]\n     \u2502  \u251c\u2500 T_SeqScan \u2192 ExecEndSeqScan() \u2014 close scan state\n     \u2502  \u251c\u2500 T_HashJoin \u2192 ExecEndHashJoin() \u2014 free hash table memory\n     \u2502  \u251c\u2500 T_Agg \u2192 ExecEndAgg() \u2014 flush final aggregates\n     \u2502  \u2514\u2500 ... [cleanup for each node type]\n     \u2502\n     \u2514\u2500 Recursively ExecEndNode(child_planstate)\n        \u2514\u2500 Release memory, file handles, etc.\n```\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n#### 1. **Pipeline/Dataflow Architecture**\nThe query execution is organized as a strict pipeline with clear stages:\n- **Parse**: Syntax validation and raw AST production\n- **Analyze**: Semantic validation and reference resolution\n- **Rewrite**: Rule application and query transformation\n- **Optimize**: Logical and physical optimization\n- **Execute**: Tuple production via iterator model\n\nEach stage produces well-defined intermediate data structures:\n```\nSQL String \u2192 RawStmt \u2192 Query \u2192 PlannedStmt \u2192 PlanState Tree \u2192 Tuples\n```\n\n#### 2. **Two-Phase Optimization (Separation of Concerns)**\n\n**Phase 1 - Path Generation (Logical):** `src/backend/optimizer/path/allpaths.c`\n- Generates multiple candidate execution strategies (Paths)\n- Focus: logical correctness and cost estimation\n- Dynamic programming for join order selection\n- Cost-based pruning keeps only viable alternatives\n- Output: RelOptInfo with pathlist\n\n**Phase 2 - Plan Creation (Physical):** `src/backend/optimizer/plan/createplan.c`\n- Selects best Path, converts to Plan tree\n- Maps logical operators to physical operators\n- Attaches implementation details (sort orders, output columns)\n- Line 395-414: Dispatch via `switch (best_path->pathtype)` converts Path\u2192Plan\n\n**Benefits:**\n- Cost model independent of plan generation\n- Easy to add new plan types without changing all paths\n- Clean separation between logical and physical optimization\n\n#### 3. **Volcano/Iterator Model (Push-up from Leaves)**\n\n**Initialization Phase (Bottom-up construction):**\n- ExecInitNode recursively builds state tree\n- Each node knows its specific ExecProcNode function\n- Mirrors plan tree structure in memory\n\n**Execution Phase (Top-down fetching):**\n```\nfor each result_tuple needed:\n  tup = ExecProcNode(top_node)  // Call iterator function\n  // Recursively:\n  //   ExecProcNode(top_node) \u2192 ExecNestLoop \u2192 calls ExecProcNode(children)\n  //   When all outer tuples: stop\n```\n\n**Function Pointer Dispatch (not switch statement):**\n```c\nExecSetExecProcNode(result, result->ExecProcNode);  // Line 391, execProcnode.c\n// Each node's ExecInit* sets result->ExecProcNode to node-specific function:\n// ExecSeqScan, ExecIndexScan, ExecNestLoop, ExecHashJoin, ExecAgg, etc.\n\n// At runtime:\nTupleTableSlot *slot = (*planstate->ExecProcNode)(planstate);  // Call via pointer\n```\n\n**Advantages:**\n- Minimal overhead (function pointer vs switch)\n- Natural pipelining (tuples flow up the tree)\n- Easy to plug in new node types (just add ExecInit*/Exec* functions)\n\n#### 4. **Dispatcher Pattern with Static and Dynamic Dispatch Hybrid**\n\nAt initialization time (static dispatch via switch):\n```c\nswitch (nodeTag(node)):  // Line 161, execProcnode.c\n  case T_SeqScan:\n    result = ExecInitSeqScan(...);\n    break;\n  case T_NestLoop:\n    result = ExecInitNestLoop(...);\n    break;\n  // 40+ cases\n```\n\nAt runtime (dynamic dispatch via function pointers):\n```c\n(*planstate->ExecProcNode)(planstate)  // No switch, just indirect call\n```\n\n**Benefit:** Fast initialization path uses switch (compiler can optimize), fast execution uses function pointers (cache-friendly).\n\n#### 5. **Node Type System (Tagged Union)**\nAll AST and plan node types tagged with NodeTag enum:\n```c\ntypedef enum NodeTag {\n  T_RawStmt, T_SelectStmt, T_Query, T_Plan, T_SeqScan, T_NestLoop, ...\n} NodeTag;\n\n// Every node starts with:\ntypedef struct SomeNode {\n  NodeTag type;\n  ...\n} SomeNode;\n```\n\nEnables:\n- Runtime type checking via `IsA(node, type)`\n- Polymorphic node operations (copy, compare, print)\n- Generic node traversal\n\n#### 6. **Recursive Tree Processing**\nPlan/Path trees are inherently recursive:\n- ExecInitNode recursively processes children\n- create_plan recursively processes child paths\n- ExecEndNode recursively finalizes children\n- Maximizes code reuse and maintains tree structure\n\n#### 7. **Cost-Based Optimization with Heuristic Pruning**\n\nDynamic programming with pruning (joinrels.c, allpaths.c):\n- Enumerate join orders using DP algorithm\n- At each DP step, keep only best paths for each relation subset\n- For large n, use GEQO (genetic algorithm) as fallback\n- Result: Tractable optimization despite exponential search space\n\n#### 8. **Separation of Planning from Execution**\n\nPlan nodes are immutable during execution:\n- No side effects during planning\n- Transaction semantics isolated in executor\n- Allows plan caching (prepared statements)\n- Multiple executions of same plan possible\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n**Traffic Cop (postgres.c):**\n- Receives raw SQL from client\n- Coordinates pipeline stages\n- Manages transaction context\n- Implements portal interface\n\n**Parser (parser/parser.c + lex/gram.y):**\n- Lexical analysis (flex)\n- Syntactic analysis (bison)\n- No semantic checking, no table access\n- Input: SQL string; Output: RawStmt list\n\n**Analyzer (parser/analyze.c + parse_*.c):**\n- Semantic validation\n- Name resolution (tables, columns, functions)\n- Type checking and coercion\n- Input: RawStmt; Output: Query\n\n**Rewriter (rewrite/rewriteHandler.c):**\n- Apply view expansion\n- Apply INSTEAD rules\n- Apply row-level security policies\n- Input: Query; Output: Query list (possibly expanded)\n\n**Optimizer Path Generation (optimizer/path/allpaths.c):**\n- Generate candidate access paths\n- Estimate costs using selectivity estimation\n- Consider index availability\n- Dynamic programming for join orders\n- Output: RelOptInfo with Path alternatives\n\n**Optimizer Plan Creation (optimizer/plan/createplan.c):**\n- Select best Path\n- Convert Path to Plan tree\n- Attach implementation details\n- Output: Plan tree\n\n**Executor Initialization (executor/execProcnode.c, ExecInitNode):**\n- Build state tree from plan tree\n- Set up runtime execution context\n- Initialize per-node state (buffers, cursors, etc.)\n- Output: PlanState tree with function pointers\n\n**Executor Runtime (executor/nodeXxx.c, ExecProcNode):**\n- Fetch tuples via Volcano model\n- Implement join algorithms (nested loop, merge, hash)\n- Implement grouping/aggregation\n- Implement sorting (when needed)\n- Output: TupleTableSlots with result tuples\n\n### Data Flow Description\n\n```\n1. PARSE PHASE (Traffic Cop \u2192 Parser)\n   Input:  SELECT a, b FROM table WHERE x > 5\n   Process: Lexer tokenizes \u2192 Parser builds syntax tree\n   Output: RawStmt { SelectStmt { ... } }\n\n2. ANALYZE PHASE (Traffic Cop \u2192 Analyzer)\n   Input:  RawStmt { SelectStmt { table: \"table\", ... } }\n   Process:\n     - Resolve \"table\" to RangeTableEntry (catalog lookup)\n     - Resolve \"a\", \"b\", \"x\" to actual columns\n     - Check types (b > 5 requires compatible types)\n   Output: Query {\n     rtable: [RTE for \"table\"],\n     targetList: [Var(a), Var(b)],\n     jointree: FromExpr with WHERE x > 5\n   }\n\n3. REWRITE PHASE (Traffic Cop \u2192 Rewriter)\n   Input:  Query { ... }\n   Process:\n     - Check if \"table\" is a view \u2192 if so, expand to underlying query\n     - Check for INSTEAD rules \u2192 apply if present\n     - Apply row-level security filters\n   Output: Query (possibly modified or expanded to multiple queries)\n\n4. OPTIMIZE PHASE (Phase 1: Paths)\n   Input:  Query { rtable: [...], conditions: [x > 5], ... }\n   Process:\n     - RelOptInfo for \"table\" created\n     - Generate Paths:\n       * SeqScan Path (read all rows)\n       * IndexScan Path (if index on x exists)\n     - Estimate costs based on stats\n     - Choose best Path (likely IndexScan if x > 5 is selective)\n   Output: Path tree with costs\n\n5. OPTIMIZE PHASE (Phase 2: Plans)\n   Input:  Path tree (best SeqScan or IndexScan)\n   Process:\n     - Convert Path to Plan node\n     - Attach output columns (a, b)\n   Output: Plan tree:\n     SeqScan {\n       relationName: \"table\",\n       targetList: [Var(a), Var(b)],\n       filter: (x > 5)\n     }\n\n6. EXECUTOR INIT PHASE (Executor \u2192 Init)\n   Input:  Plan tree\n   Process:\n     - ExecInitNode called recursively on plan tree\n     - For SeqScan: creates SeqScanState with scan iterator\n     - Sets SeqScanState->ExecProcNode = ExecSeqScan\n   Output: PlanState tree with function pointers set\n\n7. EXECUTOR RUN PHASE (Executor \u2192 Run)\n   Process:\n     for tuple_count > 0:\n       slot = ExecProcNode(top_planstate)  // Call ExecSeqScan\n       if slot is NULL: break\n       tuple = extract_tuple(slot)\n       send_to_client(tuple)\n\n   Inside ExecSeqScan():\n     - Read next page from buffer manager\n     - Extract next tuple matching filter (x > 5)\n     - Return tuple in TupleTableSlot or NULL when done\n\n8. Output: Result tuples sent to client\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts Between Components\n\n| Stage | Function | Input | Output | Invariants |\n|-------|----------|-------|--------|-----------|\n| Parser | `raw_parser()` | SQL string | `List<RawStmt>` | No semantic checking; may contain invalid tables/columns |\n| Analyzer | `parse_analyze_fixedparams()` | `RawStmt` | `Query` | All names resolved; types checked; references valid |\n| Rewriter | `pg_rewrite_query()` | `Query` | `List<Query>` | May expand to multiple queries; maintains semantic equivalence |\n| Optimizer | `planner()` | `Query` | `PlannedStmt` | Plan is executable; all Paths explored and best selected |\n| Executor | `ExecutorStart()` | `PlannedStmt` | `PlanState` | PlanState tree ready for iteration; ExecProcNode pointers set |\n| Executor | `ExecProcNode()` | `PlanState` | `TupleTableSlot` | Tuple or NULL; called repeatedly until NULL |\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nPostgreSQL's query execution pipeline is a sophisticated multi-stage system implementing classical compilation and execution architecture patterns. The **pipeline/dataflow design** organizes processing into well-separated stages (parse, analyze, rewrite, optimize, execute), each with clean input/output interfaces and well-defined intermediate representations (RawStmt \u2192 Query \u2192 PlannedStmt \u2192 tuples).\n\nThe **two-phase optimization** (path generation in allpaths.c + plan creation in createplan.c) cleanly separates logical optimization (which strategies are possible?) from physical optimization (which strategy is fastest?). This enables cost-based selection while maintaining code modularity and extensibility.\n\nThe **Volcano/iterator execution model** combined with **hybrid static/dynamic dispatch** achieves both simplicity and performance: initialization uses a switch statement for optimal startup, while execution uses function pointers for minimal per-tuple overhead and natural pipelining through the plan tree. The 40+ executor node types (scans, joins, aggregation, sorting, etc.) all follow this pattern, making it easy to add new node types without modifying core executor logic.",
